You can see and measure tangibles. You cannot see or measure intangibles. Despite that difference, both are real.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Home.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">2025</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">This letter is meant to give you a progress report on 2025 and, more importantly over longer time frames&#8212;plus some insights into our plans and dreams for the future.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In a rapidly changing, volatile, and uncertain world, we all want and need a home that can help anchor us.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Our mission is to provide you with such a &#8220;home.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">I believe we&#8217;ve done that for many years, and that we have the elements in place to continue doing so in 2026 and beyond.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">There are two distinct spheres to describe the progress we made in 2025&#58; </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">qualitative </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">and </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">quantitative.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Quantitative measures are straightforward and easy to measure.</font></div></div><div style="display:inline-block;max-width:7.079%;min-width:6.079%;vertical-align:top"></div><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.461%"><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Quantitatively, 2025 was a very good year. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Here are the numbers&#58; </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">First, by our consistently calculated method, the intrinsic value per share of Markel grew 12% in 2025. Over the last five years, the compound annual growth rate was 15%. Since our IPO, it has compounded annually at 16%.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We calculate that number using the same methodology year-by-year, which we share in our annual report. Different people might use different tools and techniques to calculate their own measurements of value. Our sense is that any reasonable method, when applied consistently over time, yields a rate of growth that fairly describes our long-term economic progress per share.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We think that calculation is validated by comparing it to the share price. The rate of increase in the share price correlates highly with our calculation of intrinsic value over long periods of time. The market seems to agree.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">While the share price and intrinsic value per share experience volatility in the short run, and might become detached from one another at times, our longer-term experience is these two values travel together&#59; and so, provide you with a dependable indication of the rate of our underlying quantitative, economic progress.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Further, the return of our stock price since our IPO ranks us in the top tier for public companies over that period.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We are proud of these long-term results, and we hope you share our pride and comfort in the compounding of capital we&#8217;ve produced in your &#8220;home.&#8221;</font></div><div 0;text-align:right;vertical-align:bottom"></td></tr></table></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Markel Insurance</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Qualitatively, 2025 was a year of productive change and recommitment in our largest business, Markel Insurance. Most notably, in March 2025, we promoted Simon Wilson to serve as CEO. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">As Simon stated, his goal is to build &#8220;the preeminent specialty insurance company on the planet.&#8221; Go Simon!</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Among other actions so far, he led a reorganization to ensure that each element of our insurance operations has its own profit and loss statement with one, and only one, accountable &#8220;owner&#8221; of each P&#38;L.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Over the nearly one hundred years of Markel&#8217;s existence, we&#8217;ve moved between poles of individual versus collective decision making. Different environments and circumstances call for different structures. No one system is, or ever will be, perfect.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Our job as business leaders is to be sensitive to the pluses and minuses of different approaches at any given time&#8212;and to adjust and adapt as necessary.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We became too centralized in our insurance operations in recent years and, as a result, there was a decline in accountability around our costs and results. Underwriting and claims decisions moved too far away from the front line. Our focus became too internal and not centered on the customer as much as it should have been.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Simon continues to move decisions, authority, and accountability closer to the customer.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">These efforts should speed up decision making, increase responsiveness, and provide clearer and faster feedback loops. That will help us make decisions with a better sense of what&#8217;s working and what&#8217;s not. Our improved decisions should improve, </font></div></div></div><div style="height:36pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:36pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="width:100.000%"><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.460%"><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">with a time lag, the financial results flowing from them.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Early results look promising.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In 2025, we grew top-line revenues and bottom-line profits across Markel Insurance. With better visibility and accountability, we also cut back or eliminated lines where we did not produce acceptable results.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We continued to see healthy growth overseas. Our International division, previously headed by Simon and now by Andrew McMellin, produced a spectacular combined ratio of 83% in 2025 and growth in written premiums of 14%. This continues our multi-year trend of excellent results in this division.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">There are so many people to thank for the wonderful International results. A very partial list includes&#58; Rohan Davies, David Sawyer and Tom Hillier in London. David Crozier in Canada, Lee Mooney in the UK, Frederik Wulff in Germany, Max Robbie in Dubai and Deepika Mathur in India. Andy Davies and Jo Browning have been crucial members of the London-based executive team supporting Andrew McMellin. There should also be special mention for Christian Stobbs who moved from his Asia Pacific role to become the strategy leader for Markel Insurance overall and has had a significant role in the transformation of the insurance business. Thank you to all of you, and to your teammates around the world. You continue to help power Markel Group&#8217;s growth and profitability. I&#8217;m excited and grateful for your work in doing so.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We also enjoy several bright spots within our US operations. Wendy Houser has re-organized and re-energized our critical Wholesale and Specialty operations from the ground up in a short period of time&#59; the feedback from our people and our brokers is tremendously positive. Our binding business that was built by Mark Schauss and Brendan Hanley continues to produce a fantastic experience for our broker customers and excellent returns for Markel. Alex Martin has organized our Programs and Solutions division in a way where results are easy to see and capital can be allocated more precisely. Jeff May and his Personal Lines team continued a multiyear streak of hard-earned and excellent results achieving a spectacular combined ratio of 82% and 16% growth in written premiums in 2025. Jim Hinchley has taken on the leadership of our Workers Comp and Small Commercial business and has quickly put in place an ambitious plan to grow in a business which continues to produce excellent results.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">With new leadership, accountability, responsibility, and structures firmly in place, I am optimistic that </font></div></div><div style="display:inline-block;max-width:7.079%;min-width:6.079%;vertical-align:top"></div><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.461%"><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">the improvements in our overall insurance operations to date will accelerate in 2026 and beyond.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In the shorter run, tougher economic conditions and softer property insurance prices may pressure reported results. I am confident, though, that our insurance business will continue to produce impressive profitability in the years to come.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Also, we will continue with our consistent goal of setting reserves that are more likely to be redundant than deficient.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">For example, Markel Insurance reported reserve redundancies in 2025 of $484 million, or 5.8 points on our combined ratio. That continues our long streak of conservative reserving. We&#8217;ve now reported reserve redundancies to you for the last twenty one years in a row. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We believe that this demonstrated conservatism and &#8220;balance sheet first&#8221; mentality reinforces the sturdiness and durability of our home. Conservative reserving is like building a home on bedrock, rather than shifting sands.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Also in 2025, we sold the renewal rights of our reinsurance operations.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">This move was part of our larger intention to refocus on our core Specialty underwriting, where we have distinct competitive advantages. After years of trying to improve the Reinsurance business, we determined that getting it to adequate returns of capital would require significant investment in scale. We saw better and higher uses of capital across the Markel Group system. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">As such, after an extensive process and a review of available alternatives, we decided to sell the renewal rights.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We believe that the remaining reserves attached to our reinsurance business are conservatively stated and we expect to earn investment income as we run off reserves over the next several years.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">While the wind down of our reinsurance business will reduce total revenues and create temporary headwinds for our expense ratio, it should improve the Markel Insurance combined ratio and return on equity, all other things constant. That should improve the overall economics of Markel Group.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Regarding our fixed income investments, they earned a total return of 3.5% in 2025&#59; we generated $733 million in net interest income within Markel Insurance and $814 million across Markel Group. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">To reiterate our bedrock philosophy, under which we&#8217;ve operated for decades&#58; we first invest in enough high-quality fixed income instruments to more than cover our insurance reserve liabilities.</font></div></div></div><div style="height:36pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:36pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="width:100.000%"><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.460%"><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We purchase the highest-quality fixed income securities we can find, and we do not take risks like the currently popular &#8220;private credit&#8221; options or riskier credit securities.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We want our fixed income &#8220;credits&#8221; to be &#8220;creditable&#8221; sources of funding when it comes time to pay claims. We don&#8217;t stretch for extra basis points of yield that might jeopardize that in any way, shape, or form.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">To complete the discussion of our insurance results, I&#8217;d like to offer you an updated chart that we debuted in last year&#8217;s annual letter.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Our &#8220;Total &#8216;Spread&#8217;&#8221; chart displays the combination of underwriting profits, plus the associated investment income we earn while holding the float generated by the insurance operations.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The cumulative positive spread from underwriting profits and interest income exceeds $11.5 billion over the last twenty one years.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In 2005, the first our existing operations, acquiring  new insurance and non-insurance businesses, publicly-traded equity securities, and Markel shares.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font><br></font></div></div><div style="display:inline-block;max-width:7.079%;min-width:6.079%;vertical-align:top"></div><div I believe that our unique design of compounding capital through disciplined reinvestment decisions, guided by our unique culture and architectural design, will continue to power these results in the years and decades ahead.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Financials</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%"> </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In 2025, our Financials businesses produced revenues of $737 million compared to $593 million in 2024 and adjusted operating income of $327 million compared to $262 million in 2024. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Matt Freeman and his team at State National and Greg Hagood, Frank Majors, and Jess Laird, and their team at Nephila, continue to operate profitable businesses of scale with substantial avenues for growth. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">State National has been a leader in the insurance fronting industry for decades. I&#8217;m very proud of the leaders and teams operating these businesses.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">As 2025 progressed, the economic conditions facing these businesses got tougher.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Economic activity within industrial end-markets slowed, as the overall economy bifurcated along a &#8220;K-shaped&#8221; path. Some businesses with exposure to boom-like spending on AI grew (the up-and-to-the-right part of the &#8220;K&#8221;). Other businesses facing tougher end-market cycles tracked the less favorable part of the &#8220;K.&#8221; We own businesses on both branches of the K, and our aggregate results reflect that reality. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The costs of labor, materials, and doing business amidst increasing complexity, continued to increase in 2025. Also, 2025 results faced difficult comparisons to some &#8220;white hot&#8221; 2024 results. The transportation equipment supercycle upswing we enjoyed over the last few years continued to unwind in 2025. This is an example of normal and expected cyclicality.</font></div></div><div style="display:inline-block;max-width:7.079%;min-width:6.079%;vertical-align:top"></div><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.461%"><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In absolute terms, 2025 was a wonderful year. It stands as the best year we&#8217;ve ever experienced in revenue, and third best on adjusted operating income, from these businesses. Danny Zink, Tommy Clements, Rick Pennell, Elliot Germany, and so many others continue to lead their businesses in ways that make me proud. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Despite the headwinds of challenging economic, regulatory, and other conditions, the Industrials segment produced attractive returns on capital and, after providing for all their capital expenditures and working capital needs, sent dividends of $145 million up to the holding company.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Within the construct and design of the Markel Group, this is an excellent example of how our strategy and architecture combine to produce excellent returns to our shareholders over time.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Our managers know that their first job is to run their businesses as if they were long-term owners&#8212;and will always remain so. We don&#8217;t lever up these businesses with debt, given that that could create short-term pressures to generate cash at inopportune times. We don&#8217;t pressure the managers to hit unrealistic budgets either. Not when conditions change, nor ever.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">As such, we don&#8217;t need to contort ourselves and make short-term &#8220;sales&#8221; at the expense of long-term results.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We support the CEOs of all our operating businesses as they seek to make the best long-term decisions they possibly can. In the interim, we seek to use the cash flows the businesses produce to repurchase Markel Group shares, make public equity investments, or acquire other attractive insurance or non-insurance businesses.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Low amounts of leverage and this &#8221;360-degree view&#8221; of capital allocation opportunities provide us with unique competitive advantages. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">2025 showed how it all works together.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Thank you to the thousands of teammates who helped contribute to these results. She enlisted her children as part of the wrapping team and made things work with an amazing attitude and work ethic.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Debra, through some of her early travel as an exchange student, also had a lifelong passion for cultural exchange and what all of us could learn from studying other cultures.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">In a magic combination of all the ingredients of Debra&#8217;s life, she started a company called Educational Partners International (EPI) in her hometown of Swannanoa, North Carolina in 2006. The teachers share their culture and knowledge with the school children. The children learn about something that they otherwise might not ever have experienced, and the school systems are better off.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Win-win-win.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We&#8217;ve been as impressed with their financial results as we have with their people.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">More importantly, those results were achieved against a backdrop of unexpected challenges.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Namely&#58; Swannanoa, North Carolina suffered some of the worst damages imaginable during Hurricane Helene. The office of EPI was completely destroyed by the flood. Many of the EPI team members were severely affected. Additionally, we continued our ongoing share repurchase program by buying 223,000 shares at an average cost of $1,894 per share during the year. We&#8217;ve now reduced our outstanding share count from approximately 14 million in 2016 down to 12.6 million at the beginning of 2026.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We also redeemed all our preferred stock ($600 million) in 2025 and made net new fixed income purchases of $1.4 billion and net new equity security purchases of $143 million. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">All these actions and numbers speak to the underlying profitability and balance sheet strength of your company.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The main reason that I am pleased with the returns is because of the way they were earned&#58; with discipline and rigor. They were earned with the awareness that not all markets are like what we&#8217;ve experienced in 2025 (and in the last few years).</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">While some investors will run faster over the sprint distances of a year or three, we operate as if we are running a marathon. We invest to avoid permanent capital loss, knowing that is way more important in the ongoing compounding and safety of your capital than winning any annual performance derby. In our equity investments, we look for publicly traded securities that meet our time-tested, four-part test. To restate those parts, we (1) invest in businesses with good returns on capital that use minimal debt, with (2) management teams with equal measures of talent and integrity, with (3) the opportunity to reinvest in their businesses and&#47;or capital discipline as evidenced by successful acquisitions, dividends, or share repurchases, and (4) pay fair prices.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Those four lenses have guided us for decades, and I think the principles are effective. Shorter-term investors may use different techniques or filters but as long-term investors, we believe in these principles.</font></div></div></div><div style="height:36pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:36pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="width:100.000%"><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.460%"><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">As of 2025, our total unrealized gain on our equity investment portfolio stands at $8.9 billion. The unrealized gain exceeds the market capitalization of all Markel Group up until 2016. I believe that number might be the second highest total for unrealized gains of any US public company.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Setting aside the emotional or pride factor of that silver medal, that means at a 22% tax rate we have a deferred tax liability of nearly $2 billion on our balance sheet. That is in essence a zero-cost loan from the government, earning a positive return and helping to compound your capital.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Returning to the &#8220;home&#8221; analogy, that unrealized gain is like solar panels on our roof producing more electricity than we use. Our electric bill is zero for that $8.9 billion chunk of our capital.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">This is a tremendous and growing economic advantage for our shareholders.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Home</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%"> </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">As Ted Lasso said, &#8220;I believe in believe.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">I use that word repeatedly. I mean it both as an assertion and an invocation.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">I believe our structure and our commitment to the long game sets us apart&#8212;and does so in a financially advantageous way.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Further, our structure works.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">I hope, after you study the evidence of our long-term performance, you will share the same conclusion.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Our structure is uncommon among publicly traded companies.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We own a collection of wonderful businesses across many industries. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">While it is accurate to state that we started with insurance, it&#8217;s also accurate to frame it another way. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">What we really started with was an idea of how to solve a customer problem.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The original customer problem stemmed from </font></div></div><div style="display:inline-block;max-width:7.079%;min-width:6.079%;vertical-align:top"></div><div style="display:inline-block;vertical-align:top;width:46.461%"><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">changes in technology that brought the automobile and the truck into daily life. They were new, and trucks caused bigger accidents (and losses) than horses. Somebody needed to figure out how to handle those bigger problems. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Our history stemmed directly from the original actions taken by Sam Markel in 1930. Observe what someone needs, see if you can figure out a way to supply that need, and build a business by doing so.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">That idea continues to power us today.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We&#8217;ve evolved over the decades from providing insurance as an agent, to underwriting those insurance risks as underwriters, to investing those insurance proceeds, to transforming those same investment principles and customer service ideas into owning financial services, industrial, and commercial businesses in whole.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The opportunity to continue to do so strikes me as an endless one.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We continue to build a </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">home</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%"> for people dedicated to serving other people.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">No technology will ever replace the basic human need to serve and be served.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">I am honored and grateful for the opportunity to play a part in the nearly hundred-year history of Markel. </font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Thank you for your role as a customer, associate, and shareholder.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">On behalf of my partners Simon Wilson, Andrew Crowley, Brian Costanzo, Richard Grinnan, and so many more of us who guide your company&#8217;s daily actions&#58; thank you.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">I hope you have found your home.</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Respectfully submitted</font></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><img alt="signature.jpg" src="signature.jpg" style="height:54px;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:180px"></div><div style="margin-top:6pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Thomas S. Gayner, </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Tahoma',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Chief Executive Officer</font></div></div></div><div style="height:36pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div></div></div></body></html>
